It is now my great honor to invite His Excellency Li Qiang, Premier of the State Council of the People's Republic of China, to deliver his remarks. Premier Li, the floor is yours. Your Excellencies, co-chair Andre Hoffman and president Alois Zwinggi, Your Excellencies leaders of participating countries, Your Excellencies heads of international organizations, distinguished business leaders, distinguished guests, ladies and gentlemen. Good morning. It's my great pleasure to join you, friends both old and new, here in the beautiful city of Dalian for the Annual Meeting of the New Champions 2026. On behalf of the Chinese government, I wish to extend warm congratulations on the opening of the meeting and express heartfelt thanks to you all for your long-standing, strong support for China's economic development. The theme of this year's meeting, "Innovating at Scale," points to a critical factor in global economic development today. As President Xi Jinping noted, innovation drives development, and innovation shapes the future. Let me take this opportunity of today's gathering to share with you China's innovation stories and offer some thoughts on global innovation cooperation based on China's economic development practice. I have three thoughts here. My first thought is: Entering the 15th Five-Year Plan, China's economy has made new headway while navigating a changing situation. The year 2026 marks the launch of China's 15th Five-Year Plan for economic and social development. Since the beginning of this year, there has been increased volatility in the international landscape as geopolitical conflicts erupted one after another. Global economic recovery, fragile as it was, has now come under greater strain. Against this backdrop, China's economy got off to a good start. It withstood the challenges, forged ahead, and demonstrated stronger resilience and a promising outlook. The overall performance can be summarized in four keywords. Keyword number one: Stability. China's economy grew by 5% in Q1 and has maintained a sound momentum in Q2. We are seeing growth in corporate profits, a moderate rebound in prices, and continued improvement in people's livelihoods. Stability may not seem like much on an ordinary day. However, when China's economy, at a massive volume of 140 trillion RMB yuan, continues to register steady and healthy growth despite the shocks of global energy shortages and severe supply chain disruptions—and when it continues to bring much-needed certainty to this increasingly uncertain world, playing a vital role as a safe harbor—such solid and robust stability is all the more precious. Keyword number two: Innovation. I bet you are aware that after years of endeavor and accumulation, China has become a hub of rapidly emerging new technologies, new products, and new business models. In the first half of this year, multiple types of commercial rockets have been successfully launched, and technologies such as quantum information, integrated circuits, and nuclear fusion have been advancing at an accelerated pace. Most notably, the AI sector has seen explosive growth. Several major AI models have reached new milestones in performance, and our daily token usage hit several hundred trillion by the end of May, which ranked first in the world. Additionally, embodied intelligence has moved into large-scale commercial application. With brilliant frontier innovations quickly sparking a sweeping transformation of growth drivers, China's economy has taken on a new look and gained renewed energy. Keyword number three: Dynamism. China's super-sized market continues to unleash demand potential, especially in services, green, and new types of consumption. Tourism, performing arts, and sports events easily draw large crowds, with tickets often sold out in seconds. Consumer favorites such as smartwatches, smart glasses, and other smart devices have seen sales multiply. In addition, here in China, flows of people, goods, information, and capital are highly vibrant. Over 550 million express deliveries are handled per day. That is more than the total of all other countries combined. All these are vivid footnotes to the certain vitality of China's economy. They are also the true reflections of the dynamism of the Chinese market, and they embody the rich diversity and high growth potential of China's domestic demand. Keyword number four: Integration. At a time of rising unilateralism and protectionism, China remains as committed as ever to opening up further. We have extended zero-tariff policies to 63 countries. We have stayed as the world's second-largest import market for 17 years running. In the first five months of this year, we recorded import growth of 20.5%, which is significantly higher than our export growth. Since last year, we have also launched a number of "export to China" promotional events to make available more channels for high-quality foreign products to enter the Chinese market. This has been well received by countries around the world. What I want to stress here is that for China, our integrated development with the world has never been an expediency, but a strategic decision made in line with the trend of history and based on our own development philosophy. In pursuing development, China does not seek to move faster by going alone. Rather, we want win-win cooperation with everyone in the world so that we can go far together. These four keywords—stability, innovation, dynamism, and integration—together present a comprehensive outlook of China's economy. They sketch out both the current picture and the future trajectory. We are confident and capable of sustaining and harnessing this strong momentum so as to keep writing new chapters in China's high-quality development. That is my first thought. My second thought is: Innovation-driven development is the key to China's long-term steady and sustained economic success. Over the years, China's economy has maintained steady and healthy development, and I think this can be attributed to two critical factors: namely, the stable environment and the strength of innovation. The stable environment in China, I believe, is widely recognized, and many of you know this from personal experience, so I will not elaborate here. As for the strength of innovation, the visible outcomes and vibrant activities tend to attract more attention, while the strenuous efforts and long-time dedication that contributed to those successes are not always fully appreciated. In this connection, I wish to underscore three key messages. Message number one: China's innovation has been forged through relentless, painstaking effort. We are well aware that there are no shortcuts in sci-tech research, and no one can copy their way to an innovation edge. There has to be solid, hard work to tackle tough challenges. In recent years, in order to achieve greater self-reliance and strength in science and technology, we have steadily increased input into sci-tech research. During the 14th Five-Year Plan period from 2021 to 2025, our total R&D expenditure grew by an average of 10% annually, making China the world's second-largest R&D spender. Last year, basic research accounted for more than 7% of total R&D expenditure, setting a new record in history. During this process, Chinese enterprises have done an amazing job, demonstrating unyielding resilience and steadfast dedication. Many industry leaders have endured operational pressures brought about by prolonged and costly R&D commitments. Some incurred heavy losses at certain stages, and others faced unfair external suppression. Despite all this, none of them ever wavered in their commitment, and their perseverance has finally paid off. One typical example is Huawei. The company has suffered financially under technological blockade. But instead of cutting costs on R&D, we have learned that Huawei invested over 1 trillion RMB yuan in research over a period of nearly ten years. It is thanks to this substantial input into R&D that Huawei achieved a host of breakthroughs in hard-core technology. This year marks the start of the 15th Five-Year Plan, and during this period that ends in 2030, we will further strengthen research on key technologies. We will significantly raise the proportion of basic research funding. We will continuously enhance the capacity for original innovation. All this will provide an inexhaustible source of energy for the innovation and high-quality development of China's economy. That is my first message: that China's innovation has been forged through relentless, painstaking effort. My second message is that China's innovation has been tempered through extensive applications across multiple industries. Science and technology thrive in application. The most difficult leap in innovation is often not the one inside the lab, but the one across the Darwinian sea that separates the lab from the market. The key, therefore, lies in better connecting science and technology with industry. After years of pursuing innovation-driven development, China has blazed a successful path by which sci-tech innovation spearheads industrial innovation, and industrial upgrades propel sci-tech evolution. On the one hand, rapid sci-tech progress is the wellspring of industrial development. In recent years, we have made active explorations in frontier and emerging sectors and achieved a large volume of innovation outcomes that have given birth to many new industries. As you know, the vigorous growth of China's new energy and intelligent connected vehicle industries, for example, has been enabled by our sci-tech breakthroughs in new materials, power batteries, and communications technology. These innovations, not government subsidies as some have speculated, are the core competitiveness of Chinese products. We do not have enough money to do all these subsidies, to be very frank. It is mainly because of the big market for these new products, and our development in science and technology has been the wellspring of industrial development, as I have stressed. On the other hand, China's massive application scenarios provide a powerful incubator and training ground for new technologies. China has a complete industrial system and a big market. So, a promising sci-tech outcome backed by China's manufacturing strength can be rapidly turned into real-world consumer goods. Likewise, a niche product placed in a market of 1.4 billion consumers has the potential to grow into a sizable business and even a big industry. Last evening, I learned from the news that at the China International Supply Chain Expo, one exhibitor said to the press during an interview that in his country, the period from invention to real-world application would take one whole year. But in Shenzhen, it took only one week to turn that blueprint into real-world products. He may have been just polite because he was in China. But to be frank, our strong manufacturing industry, as well as our strong and complete industrial system, can turn even a very niche product into real-world products. That is our strength. So, with broad participation across all sectors, with frequent feedback from countless users, and with repeated refinement across diverse scenarios, new technologies have been able to evolve and upgrade continuously through large-scale application. Going forward, we will promote deeper integration between sci-tech innovation and industrial innovation. We will expand effective domestic demand. We will accelerate the large-scale application of new technologies and products. We will also strengthen the mutually reinforcing cycle of sci-tech advances and industrial development. That is my second message. My third message is that China's innovation has been nurtured in an enabling environment. Innovation today, as you know, is highly complex and systemic, requiring larger-scale resource input, stronger supporting measures, and a more enabling institutional environment. For years, China has worked hard to enhance its systemic innovation capacity and has achieved remarkable results. We have been increasing support in resources and factors of production, putting in place a diversified investment system with enterprises leading the way, the government providing guidance, and society participating. Now, R&D investment by enterprises accounts for nearly 80% of China's total R&D spending. Our enterprises are really incredible and forward-looking. We have also been building a batch of major sci-tech research facilities and infrastructure, training some 7 million university graduates in science, engineering, agriculture, and medicine every year. We have prioritized building innovation platforms. Of the world's top 100 innovation clusters, 24 are in China, topping the Global Innovation Index ranking for three consecutive years. Professional, differentiated, and specialized industrial clusters are spread across the country. These range from the one-hour electronic information innovation circle in the Yangtze River Delta and the one-hour motorcycle industrial circle in Chongqing, to the 30-minute supporting circle in Shenzhen's Robot Valley. These platforms have incubated a large number of high-tech enterprises, as well as "little giants" that use specialized and sophisticated technologies to produce novel and unique products. Moreover, we have deepened our institutional reform in science and technology, putting in place more effective mechanisms for intellectual property protection and sci-tech outcomes transfer. We have also worked hard to foster a culture of innovation that encourages experimentation and tolerates failure. All these have combined to create a fertile soil for innovation to sprout and flourish. That is my third message: that China's innovation has been nurtured in an enabling environment. We are also advancing reforms of systems and institutions, introducing a series of new policies and new measures in intellectual property rights protection, risk-sharing, innovation incentives, and other areas. Going forward, we will continue to improve the innovation ecosystem and speed up the development of infrastructure, including new-type power grids, computing power networks, and new-generation telecommunications networks. This will effectively remove barriers to better resource allocation and keep unlocking and unleashing the innovation dynamism of the whole society. China's rapidly growing innovation capacity has been widely welcomed and recognized by most in the world. Some, however, respond differently. They are anxious about China's sci-tech and industrial innovation, and for various reasons, even come up with some unfriendly narratives. For instance, the so-called "China shock 2.0" as reported by some media outlets. They claim China's development is a shock to the world. But as I have noticed, in the recent discussions about this narrative by some institutions and media outlets, there are more mentions of an opposite term: namely, "China opportunity 2.0," not "China shock 2.0." They believe China's development provides opportunities for the world. In the past, China's big market and low-cost production factors had provided market dividends for the world. Today, while continuing to provide even greater market dividends, China is also offering more and more innovation dividends with its technological progress and industrial upgrading. What these combined dividends generate for the world are greater opportunities and potential for development. For enterprises around the world, "China opportunity 2.0" means across-the-board innovation empowerment and high-return investment opportunities. As we have seen, a growing number of foreign enterprises have come to China to set up research centers and regional headquarters, becoming deeply integrated into China's innovation and industrial chains. This is a clear shift from "made in China" to "created in China." In 2023, 14,000 foreign-funded enterprises were established in the fields of scientific research and technological services, up by 27.2% year-on-year. Here in China, enterprises from various countries can quickly find whole-process partners from R&D to prototyping and mass production, making innovation easier and more efficient. This not only helps companies succeed in the Chinese market but also boosts their global competitiveness. At the same time, fast-growing Chinese innovative enterprises can also generate returns for investors across the world that could be several or even dozens of times the original capital. This reminds me of my hometown, Hangzhou. There is a very popular company called Unitree, and we can see the performance of their robots. Ten years ago, or more than ten years ago, when I was the governor of Zhejiang Province, Unitree was still a small company. When I left Zhejiang in 2016, the company was valued at just over 10 million RMB yuan. But now, the company is worth 42 billion yuan. That is a several-thousand-fold increase in just ten years' time. The number of Chinese enterprises with such potential is still growing, not just Unitree. Recent months have seen a faster flow of global capital into China's technology assets. For global development, "China opportunity 2.0" means more accessible advanced technologies and widely shared outcomes. China is committed to an open approach to innovation. Much of its innovation is open-source. This enables more countries, particularly developing countries, to access affordable new technologies and new products, which has enhanced their development capacity and can help address many difficulties holding back global development. Today, China's large open-source AI models have been downloaded over 10 billion times globally in cumulative terms. Large-scale scientific facilities in controlled nuclear fusion, quantum technology, and other areas are open to the world. The Tiangong space station is also set to welcome foreign astronauts, as you may have seen in relevant media reports. These are proof enough that what China's technologies and products in emerging areas bring to the world are not shocks or threats, but opportunities and empowerment. And this is my second thought. My third thought is that innovation cooperation is an imperative for tackling the global growth predicament. Throughout China's development, innovation has played an irreplaceable and pivotal role. In the broader global economy, it stands as a vital pathway to counter downward pressure and reignite growth momentum. At present, global innovation activities have taken on new characteristics and trends unlike anything seen before. First, never before has technology advanced so fast, but the risks of losing control are notably rising. In particular, AI has vastly enhanced innovation efficiency, with breakthroughs emerging on all frontiers. Some call this the Cambrian moment of the intelligent age. But we have to see that the risks of losing control and ethical lapses are also mounting in the new landscape. Without commensurate governance, the fallout could be severe. Second, never before has innovation been so deeply interconnected, yet the barriers to collaboration are increasing. Collective efforts that cross disciplines and national borders have become the mainstream and necessity of innovation. Yet technological walls, barriers, and blockades are also growing more pervasive in some parts of the world. I believe innovation that truly transforms and benefits the world must always open up to and embrace the world. In this new landscape, only through stronger cooperation can we generate more breakthroughs, and only through stronger cooperation can we rise to the diverse risks and challenges before us. We should deepen connectivity and collaboration to build greater synergy for innovation. In this new round of technological revolution and industrial transformation, no country or company can succeed alone. An interconnected global market enables more efficient flow and allocation of production factors and significantly reduces innovation costs. An inclusive and collaborative innovation network allows ideas to interact and converge more freely, accelerating breakthroughs in frontier technologies. China will integrate more proactively into the global innovation and industrial chains, work with all sides to build an open world economy, jointly safeguard stable and smooth global industrial and supply chains, foster more innovation outcomes, and strengthen the drivers of growth. We should harness technology for good and more effectively advance collective governance. Innovation drives humanity's quest for a better life. Advanced technologies should serve as tools that benefit people across countries rather than sources of chaos that undermine peace and stability. This calls for better coordination between development and security and a joint effort to improve global governance, so that technological progress always reflects humanity's common values and advances global peace and development. China will continue to participate in global governance in AI and other areas in a responsible and constructive manner. We will work with all sides to improve rules, enhance regulatory effectiveness, mitigate risks, and better promote shared development. Ladies and gentlemen, friends, enterprises are the principal force of innovation, and entrepreneurs bear the key responsibilities of making it happen. I encourage you to be pioneers of innovation. Look beyond today's contested red oceans toward the vast blue oceans ahead. Use innovation to expand the global market pie and to win the future for your businesses. I encourage you to be champions of win-win cooperation. Support, join, and advance global innovation cooperation. Tear down walls and build bridges. Generate fresh ideas through exchange and grow together by enabling each other's success. I encourage you to stay the course with China and put down deeper roots in this market. No matter how the world changes, China's door will only open wider. We will expand market access, fully enforce national treatment for foreign enterprises, and keep fostering a world-class business environment. We warmly welcome businesses from around the world to China to invest and do business here, share in the new opportunities we offer, and join us in building a brighter future. To conclude, I wish this year's annual meeting a full success. Thank you. Premier Li, your speech has set a thoughtful and forward-looking tone for this Annual Meeting of New Champions. At a time of deep transformation in the global economy, your reflections on innovation, openness, cooperation, and shared development are both timely and highly relevant. The reiteration of China's continued opening up and China's call for multilateralism and global cooperation will continue providing opportunities for global communities. Premier Li, thank you once again for joining us today and for sharing your vision with this international community. Ladies and gentlemen, please join me in thanking His Excellency Premier Li Qiang, and the opening plenary is now concluded.

Special Address by Kim Minseok, Prime Minister of the Republic of Korea

World Economic Forum(1.1M)·40:16·624 views·2026-06-24
Kim MinseokPrime Minister of the Republic of Korea
TL;DRSouth Korea is executing a bold economic paradigm shift to become a Top 3 global AI powerhouse and the world leader in physical AI.
To ensure this transformation benefits humanity equitably, the nation is establishing a multilateral Global AI Hub and experimenting with...

TL;DR

South Korea is executing a bold economic paradigm shift to become a Top 3 global AI powerhouse and the world leader in physical AI. To ensure this transformation benefits humanity equitably, the nation is establishing a multilateral Global AI Hub and experimenting with progressive social policies, including basic income schemes.

The Dual Engines of Growth: AI and Energy Transformation

  • The Need for a New Paradigm: Prime Minister Kim Minseok noted that South Korea has transitioned from a historical aid recipient to a developed aid donor. However, because traditional economic models have reached their potential growth limits, the country must pivot toward innovation-driven growth.
  • Dual Transition Strategy: The government is focusing heavily on two parallel transformations:
    • AI Transformation (AIX): Integrating AI across all manufacturing and service industries.
    • Energy Transition: Overhauling the electricity grid and power systems to support the massive energy demands of AI data centers, a shift accelerated by geopolitical instability in the Middle East.
  • Ambitious AI Targets:
    • Top 3 Powerhouse: South Korea aims to secure a position as one of the top three AI nations globally.
    • Physical AI Dominance: Leveraging its world-class manufacturing, semiconductor, and ICT infrastructures, the country plans to become the global leader in physical AI.
    • Hardware Security: The country has proactively secured more than 260,000 GPUs to support its domestic computational needs.

National Policy and Institutional Frameworks

  • Record R&D Investment: Under the current administration, South Korea has expanded its national R&D budget to record-high levels, specifically targeting basic science and fundamental technology development.
  • Proactive Regulation and Strategy:
    • National AI Strategy Committee: Established in September 2023 directly under the President to coordinate national efforts.
    • AI Basic Act: South Korea has streamlined its institutional frameworks by enacting the world's second-ever AI Basic Act.
    • APEC AI Initiative: Led the adoption of this regional initiative as a summit-level outcome during the APEC meeting in Gyeongju.

Establishing the "Global AI Hub" in Korea

  • A Multilateral Open Platform: In collaboration with international organizations (including UN agencies like the ILO, WHO, and IMO, as well as multilateral development banks), South Korea has officially launched plans to host the Global AI Hub.
    • Signing Partners: Nine international organizations recently traveled to Seoul to sign the official agreement.
    • Timeline: Project implementation begins this year, with detailed operational plans rolling out next year.
  • Solving Global Challenges: Under the slogan "AI to Solve Global Challenges," the hub will utilize AI models and shared knowledge to address systemic global crises such as infectious diseases, climate change, and food security.
  • Bridging the AI Divide: The hub is explicitly designed to prevent tech-monopolies. It will provide education, training, and infrastructure support to developing countries, SMEs, and young global talent.

Mitigating AI Risks through Progressive Social Policy

  • Addressing Job Displacement and Inequality: Acknowledging the "dark shadow" of rapid technological breakthroughs, the Prime Minister emphasized that South Korea's transition must be inclusive.
  • The Corporate Wealth Debate: The AI boom has triggered massive stock gains for South Korean semiconductor giants. This has sparked intense national debate over whether these profits should solely benefit corporate shareholders or be shared with the public, given that these firms heavily benefited from taxpayer-funded government support.
  • Universal Basic Income Experiments: South Korea is actively preparing for future AI-driven wealth distribution by testing economic safety nets:
    • Local Currency Pilots: The government is currently piloting basic income programs in rural communities using localized currencies.
    • Policy-Level Discourse: The Prime Minister revealed that South Korea's cabinet ministers maintain a dedicated, ongoing forum to discuss these social experiments, aiming to pioneer a framework where AI benefits are distributed evenly across society.

Notable Quotes

"Of all the potential AI capabilities, I believe that we are competitive in terms of physical AI development... We want to, if we want to be bold, be number one." — *Prime Minister Kim Minseok*
"In building the AI ecosystem, we are not going to pursue hegemony... Korea is not going to increase any tension. We can offer the space for everyone to participate." — *Prime Minister Kim Minseok*
"Future benefits and profits to be generated by AI may also be distributed in the format of some sort of basic income schemes... We want to be a pioneer in going through this AI transformation because basic income is all about fair and equal distribution of economic growth." — *Prime Minister Kim Minseok*
Ladies and gentlemen, excellencies and friends, let me start with an apology. I apologize for the delay. We had a meeting with Premier Li Qiang from China and a group of CEOs, and that took 30 minutes longer than we planned. Our planning was a bit short-sighted on that interaction with the premier, so apologies for the delay. It is my honor and pleasure to introduce the speaker for this session, His Excellency Kim Minseok, the 49th Prime Minister of the Republic of Korea. As one of the industrial and also cultural powerhouses, Korea's journey so far as well as its future is of great significance to the global economy. Prime Minister Kim has personally overseen some of the outstanding achievements of the current administration, which has successfully managed to put the country back on track from a period of brief political instability. Korea and its people's democratic resilience has been a strong inspiration. I'm also pleased to call him a part of the Forum family, as he was nominated as one of our Global Leaders for Tomorrow back in 2000. Mr. Prime Minister, all of us here gathered in Dalian and watching from around the world are keen to hear your remarks. Please join me in welcoming His Excellency Kim Minseok. 반갑습니다. 방금 소개받은 대한민국 국무총리 김민석입니다. 지난 2000년 다보스 포럼에서 내일의 글로벌 리더로 선정되었던 기억이 가물가물합니다. 제가 글로벌 리더였는지 모르겠습니다만, 오늘 여러분 앞에 서게 되어 매우 영광스럽고 기쁩니다. 26년 전 다보스 포럼의 안목이 매우 정확했다는 것을 새삼 느낍니다. 대한민국 국무총리로서 10년 만에 다시 하계 다보스 포럼에 참석하게 되어 감회가 남다릅니다. 이번 포럼에 초대해 주신 다보스 포럼과 세계경제포럼 관계자 여러분께 감사의 말씀을 드립니다. 하계 다보스 포럼의 정식 명칭은 '뉴 챔피언 연차 총회'입니다. 그 이름에 걸맞게 하계 다보스 포럼은 혁신을 통해 새로운 성장 기회를 모색하는 플랫폼으로 자리매김해 왔습니다. 어제와 오늘 이곳 다롄에서는 AI와 같은 첨단 기술 혁신을 통해 어떻게 더 많은 기회를 창출하고 이를 실질적이고 의미 있는 경제 성장으로 이끌어낼 것인지에 대해 심도 있는 논의가 이루어졌습니다. 오늘 저는 여러분과 함께 혁신을 통한 새로운 성장에 대한 대한민국의 비전을 공유하고자 합니다. 오늘날 세계 경제는 자국 우선주의, 보호무역주의, 공급망 불안정, 기후 위기 등 복합적인 불확실성에 직면해 있습니다. 동시에 AI와 같은 신기술의 발전은 우리에게 새로운 기회와 함께 이전에 없었던 심각한 도전 과제를 안겨주고 있습니다. 우리는 과거의 전략에만 의존해서는 이러한 도전과 불확실성을 극복할 수 없을 것입니다. 작년 6월 출범한 대한민국 이재명 정부는 이러한 거대한 전환의 시대를 돌파하기 위해 '혁신 성장'에 매진해 왔습니다. 정부는 세계 최고의 혁신 국가 건설을 주요 국정 목표 중 하나로 설정하고, 경제 패러다임의 근본적인 전환을 과감하게 추진하고 있습니다. 정부는 기초 과학과 원천 기술 개발에 투자하기 위해 R&D 예산을 역대 최대 수준으로 확대했습니다. 실패를 두려워하지 않는 과감한 연구 개발을 독려하고, R&D 결과가 실제 산업 현장에 적용될 수 있는 생태계를 조성하고 있습니다. 동시에 신산업 발전을 저해할 수 있는 규제를 선제적으로 개혁하고 있습니다. AI는 경제 및 사회 혁신의 핵심 주제입니다. 인공지능이 촉발한 거대한 변화는 우리의 일상을 뒤바꿔 놓고 있습니다. 이러한 배경 속에서 대한민국 정부는 작년 9월 대통령 직속 국가 AI 전략 위원회를 출범시켰습니다. 또한 세계에서 두 번째로 AI 기본법을 제정하여 제도적 틀을 정비했습니다. 산업 전반에 걸친 AI 전환을 촉진하는 한편, 인재 양성과 혁신 기업 육성에도 적극 나서고 있습니다. 작년 경주에서 APEC 정상회의가 개최되었습니다. 그곳에서 대한민국 정부의 주도로 'APEC AI 이니셔티브'가 정상 차원의 성과물로 채택되었습니다. 물론 급격한 기술 발전은 부작용을 낳을 수도 있습니다. 즉, 어두운 그림자를 드리울 수 있습니다. 혁신 성장의 진정한 완성은 사회 구성원 모두가 소외되지 않고 혜택을 누리는 '포용적 성장'을 통해 이루어집니다. 대한민국 정부는 혁신 주도 경제를 추진하는 동시에, 기술의 혜택이 특정 집단에 집중되지 않고 사회 전체에 고르게 분산되도록 하는 틀을 마련하는 것을 최우선 과제로 삼고 있습니다. AI 발전 과정에서 사회적 약자의 소외나 특정 지역의 발전 정체와 같은 불균형이 심화되는 것을 방지하기 위해, 대한민국은 'AI 보편적 기본 사회'와 균형 잡힌 국가 발전을 실현하기 위해 노력하고 있습니다. 우리의 노력은 대한민국 내에만 머물지 않습니다. 우리는 전 세계 시민들이 AI의 혜택을 누릴 수 있도록 '모두를 위한 AI'라는 목표를 향해 나아가고 있습니다. 이러한 노력의 일환으로 지난 5월 국제기구와 협력하여 대한민국에 '글로벌 AI 허브'를 구축하겠다는 계획을 공식 발표했습니다. 글로벌 AI 허브를 대한민국에 유치하기 위해 미국과 스위스를 방문하여 많은 관계자들을 만났고, 마침내 대한민국에 글로벌 AI 허브를 조성할 수 있게 되었습니다. 이 허브는 다양한 이해관계자가 참여하는 개방형 플랫폼이 될 것입니다. 다양한 기관, 기업, 연구소, 개인 간의 자유로운 소통과 혁신을 촉진할 것입니다. '글로벌 도전 과제 해결을 위한 AI'라는 슬로건 아래, AI를 통해 글로벌 이슈를 해결하는 거점 역할을 할 것입니다. 감염병, 기후 변화, 식량 안보 등 오늘날 세계가 직면한 위기는 개별 국가나 기관의 노력만으로는 해결할 수 없습니다. 유엔, 다양한 국제기구, 다자개발은행, 각국 정부, 기업 및 대학들이 글로벌 AI 허브에 모여 지식을 공유하고 AI 모델과 솔루션을 개발하여 이러한 글로벌 도전 과제에 대응해 나갈 것입니다. 이 과정에서 글로벌 AI 허브는 글로벌 AI 격차를 해소하는 역할도 수행할 것입니다. 개발도상국, 중소기업, 청년 인재들이 혁신의 기회에 참여하고 공유할 수 있도록 교육, 훈련, 인프라 지원을 강화할 계획입니다. 신사 숙녀 여러분, 최근 대한민국을 방문한 엔비디아 CEO 젠슨 황은 대한민국을 AI 생태계의 핵심 파트너라고 설명했습니다. AI는 알고리즘만으로 완성될 수 없습니다. 반도체, 데이터 센터, 통신 네트워크, 전력망 및 기타 인프라는 물론 AI 애플리케이션과 보안 시스템을 포함한 전체 시스템이 필요합니다. 이런 점에서 우리는 독특한 강점을 보유하고 있습니다. 세계 수준의 반도체 산업, 첨단 제조 역량, 안정적이고 고품질의 전력망, ICT 인프라, 역동적인 산업 생태계를 바탕으로 대한민국은 풀스택 AI 역량을 갖추고 있습니다. 이것이 우리 대한민국의 강점입니다. 이러한 역량을 바탕으로 대한민국은 혁신을 위한 글로벌 협력을 확대하고, 기업, 투자자, 연구자가 함께 성장할 수 있는 환경을 조성하여 AI 통해 인류의 번영에 기여하고자 합니다. '승풍파랑'이라는 말이 있습니다. 바람을 타고 파도를 헤쳐 나간다는 뜻입니다. 인류는 불확실성을 두려워하지 않고, 거대한 변화의 물결이 제공하는 기회를 포착하여 시대의 파도를 헤쳐 나갈 것입니다. 여러분의 과감한 도전과 대한민국의 역량이 결합될 때, 혁신 성장은 인류에게 번영을 안겨줄 것입니다. 그리고 그 과정에서 대한민국이 여러분과 함께할 것입니다. 다시 한번 뜻깊은 자리에 함께해 주신 여러분께 감사드립니다. 대단히 감사합니다. Good afternoon everyone. As was introduced, I'm Kim Minseok, Prime Minister of the Republic of Korea. Back in 2000 at the Davos Forum, I was nominated as a young leader for the future. I vaguely remember because it was such a long time ago. I'm not sure if I was indeed a global leader back then, but I am very honored and pleased to be standing in front of you. The prediction that the Davos Forum made 26 years ago was very accurate. It is indeed meaningful that I'm attending the Summer Davos Forum for the first time in 10 years as the Prime Minister of Korea. I'd like to thank the Davos Forum and the World Economic Forum for their invitation. The name of the Davos Summer Forum is the "Annual Meeting of the New Champions." Befitting its name, Summer Davos has developed into a platform where we seek new growth opportunities through innovation. Yesterday and today here in Dalian, intense discussions were held on how to create more opportunities through advanced technological innovation like AI, and how to lead them to substantial and meaningful economic growth. Today, I'd like to share with you Korea's vision on new growth through innovation. Today, the global economy is facing complex uncertainties involving nationalism, trade protectionism, supply chain instability, and the climate crisis. So, there are increasingly complex uncertainties. At the same time, advancement in new technology such as AI is presenting us with new opportunities on one hand, as well as serious challenges that did not exist before. We will not be able to overcome these challenges and uncertainties by relying solely on past strategies. Since taking office in June last year, the Lee Jae-myung administration of the Republic of Korea has been dedicated to innovating at scale to break through this era of grand transformation. Since setting a world-leading innovative economy as one of the primary goals of the government, we have been boldly pushing for a fundamental transition in our economic paradigm. The government has expanded its R&D budget to record-high levels to invest in basic science and fundamental technology development. We continue to encourage bold research and development without fear of failure, and create an ecosystem that allows results of R&D to be actually applied in the industry. At the same time, we're proactively reforming regulations that may hold back the development of new industries. AI is a key topic for economic and social innovation. The grand transformation triggered by artificial intelligence is upending our daily lives. Against this backdrop, the Korean government launched the National AI Strategy Committee directly under the President in September last year. We have also streamlined our institutional framework by enacting an AI Basic Act, for the second time in the world. While promoting AI transformation across the industry, we're also actively nurturing talent and innovative businesses. Last year, we had the APEC Economic Leaders' Meeting in Gyeongju. There, the APEC AI Initiative was adopted as a summit-level outcome under the leadership of the Korean government. Of course, rapid technological advancement can have problems. In other words, it can cast a dark shadow. The true fulfillment of innovating at scale is achieved through inclusive development in which all members of society benefit without being left behind. The Korean government, while promoting an innovation-driven economy, has made it a top priority to establish a framework that ensures the benefits of technology are distributed evenly across society rather than concentrated in specific groups. During the course of AI development, to prevent the deepening of imbalances such as the marginalization of the socially vulnerable or the underdevelopment of specific regions, Korea is striving to realize an AI universal basic society and balanced national development. Our efforts do not stop within Korea. We are working toward the goal of "AI for All" to ensure that all global citizens can enjoy the benefits of AI. As part of this effort, last May, in collaboration with international organizations, we officially announced plans to establish a Global AI Hub in Korea. In order to attract the Global AI Hub to Korea, I visited the US and Switzerland, where I met with many representatives. We were finally able to establish the Global AI Hub in Korea. The Hub will be an open platform involving diverse stakeholders, fostering free communication and innovation among various institutions, companies, research institutes, and individuals. Under the slogan "AI to Solve Global Challenges," it will serve as a hub for addressing global issues through AI. The crises facing the world today, such as infectious disease, climate change, and food security, cannot be resolved by the efforts of individual nations or institutions alone. The UN, various international organizations, multilateral development banks, national governments, companies, and universities will come together at the Global AI Hub to share knowledge and develop AI models and solutions to address these global challenges. In this process, the Global AI Hub will also play a role in bridging the global AI divide. We intend to strengthen education, training, and infrastructure support so that developing countries, SMEs, and young talents can participate and share in the opportunities for innovation. Ladies and gentlemen, NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huang, who recently visited Korea, described Korea as a key partner in the AI ecosystem. AI cannot be completed through algorithms alone. It requires an entire system that includes semiconductors, data centers, communication networks, power grids, and other infrastructure, as well as AI applications and security systems. In this regard, we possess unique strengths. With a world-class semiconductor industry, advanced manufacturing capabilities, a stable, high-quality power grid, ICT infrastructure, and a dynamic industrial ecosystem, Korea has full-stack AI capabilities. This is a strength of our country. Building on these capabilities, Korea aims to expand global cooperation for innovation and create an environment where companies, investors, and researchers can grow together, thereby contributing to humanity's prosperity through AI. There is a saying, "riding the wind and breaking the waves," or "Seung-pung-pa-rang." Humanity will not fear uncertainty but will seize the opportunities presented by the tide of massive change to navigate the waves of our times. When your bold challenges combine with Korea's capabilities, innovating at scale will usher in prosperity at scale. In that process, Korea will be with you. Once again, thank you all for joining us on this meaningful occasion. Thank you very much. Thank you very much, Prime Minister, and we're very grateful that you're also open to a few questions. I would like to start with the following question: In your speech, you mentioned that Korea's vision is one of an innovation-driven economy. What triggered or pursued Korea to have this vision, and what are the goals you want to pursue with that vision of an innovation-driven economy? 혁신, 그러니까 우리가 혁신 성장을 말하고 있습니다. 혁신 성장을 대한민국이 결정하게 된 배경, 그리고 그 배후에 있는 동력이 무엇인지에 대한 질문이군요. 그래서 대한민국이 왜 혁신 성장을 강조하게 되었는지, 그리고 경제 패러다임의 전환을 추진하게 된 배경이 무엇인지에 대해 말씀드리자면, 크게 두 가지 이유가 있다고 생각합니다. 첫째는 대한민국 경제 자체의 변화입니다. 2차 세계대전 이후 여러분도 기억하시겠지만 대한민국은 세계에서 가장 가난한 나라 중 하나였고 원조를 받는 나라였습니다. 하지만 이제는 원조를 주는 나라가 되었고 우리 경제도 선진화되었습니다. 대한민국은 이 정도까지 경제를 성장시킬 수 있었던 몇 안 되는 국가 중 하나입니다. 70년대와 80년대를 거치며 급격한 경제 발전을 이룩할 수 있었습니다. 하지만 다른 선진국들과 마찬가지로 이제 우리도 잠재 성장력의 한계에 직면해 있습니다. 과거에는 여러 가지 성공적인 경제 발전 모델이 있었습니다. 하지만 이러한 모델들이 과거만큼 잘 작동하지 않고 있습니다. 그래서 우리는 경제 패러다임을 바꿔야 한다는 깨달음을 얻게 되었습니다. 그것이 첫 번째 이유입니다. 둘째는 여러분도 아시다시피 AI의 발전과 함께 전 세계적인 변화가 일어나고 있다는 점입니다. 인공지능 시대에는 모든 산업이 영향을 받고 있습니다. 그리고 이 모든 산업들이 연결되어야 하며, 동시에 전력에 대한 엄청난 수요가 발생하고 있습니다. AI는 제조업뿐만 아니라 AI 데이터 센터를 위한 엄청난 수요를 창출하고 있습니다. 그래서 한편으로는 AI 전환, 즉 AIX를 추진하고 있으며, 동시에 에너지 전환의 필요성에도 직면해 있습니다. 전력망과 에너지 시스템의 전환이 필요합니다. 이 두 가지 이유로 우리는 현재 경제 패러다임의 변화를 꾀하고 있습니다. 그래서 핵심은 한편으로는 AIX, 즉 AI 전환이며 다른 한편으로는 에너지 전환입니다. 그래서 우리의 목표는 한편으로는 전 세계에서 가장 강력한 AI 3대 강국 중 하나가 되는 것입니다. 우리가 그 3대 강국 중 하나가 된다면 다른 두 나라는 어디가 될지 모르겠습니다만, 우리의 목표는 전 세계 TOP 3 AI 강국이 되는 것입니다. 그리고 AI, 특히 피지컬 AI 역량에 있어서 우리는 대담한 목표를 가지고 있습니다. 대담하게 말하자면 피지컬 AI 분야에서 세계 1위가 되고 싶습니다. 왜냐하면 우리는 매우 강력한 제조 및 산업 역량을 보유하고 있기 때문입니다. 그래서 모든 잠재적인 AI 역량 중에서 우리는 피지컬 AI 발전 측면에서 경쟁력이 있다고 믿습니다. 이제 대한민국의 현재 경제 역량을 생각해 보면, 우리는 가능한 한 많은 GPU를 확보하는 데 주력해 왔습니다. 그래서 지금까지 26만 개 이상의 GPU를 확보했는데, 이는 우리가 필요로 하는 것보다 더 많을 수도 있습니다. 동시에 우리는 재생 에너지로의 전환을 통해 전력 공급 방식을 바꾸려고 노력하고 있습니다. 물론 그 전환이 일어나기까지는 시간이 좀 걸릴 것입니다. 하지만 중동에서 전쟁이 일어나고 있는 상황에서 우리는 다시 한번 에너지 패러다임을 바꿔야 한다는 것을 깨달았습니다. 우리는 에너지 자원을 전혀 생산하지 못합니다. 수입해야 합니다. 그래서 많은 압박을 받고 있습니다. 하지만 동시에 우리는 이 위기를 기회로 바꾸고 싶습니다. 중동의 혼란으로 촉발된 이 에너지 위기는 우리가 에너지 전환을 가속화하는 기회가 될 수 있습니다. 요약하자면, 현재 혁신 주도 경제의 트리거는 우리 내부의 경제 시스템의 변화였지만, 우리는 TOP 3 AI 강국 중 하나가 되고 싶습니다. So we're talking about innovation. When it comes to innovation, Korea has decided to focus on innovation. What was the background behind our decision to focus on innovation, and what are the key drivers behind that? To address this question of the background behind Korea's emphasis on innovation and the pursuit of a shift in our economic paradigm, I believe that there are two main reasons. First of all, there have been changes in the Korean economy itself. After the Second World War, as you may remember, Korea was one of the poorest countries in the world, and we used to be an aid recipient. But now, we have become an aid donor country and our economy has been advanced. Korea is one of the few countries that have been able to grow its economy to this extent. Throughout the '70s and '80s, we were able to achieve rapid economic development. But just like other advanced economies, now we're faced with limits in our potential growth. In the past, we had several successful economic development models, but these models are not working as well as they did in the past. So, we have come to a realization that we need to change our economic paradigm. That's the first reason. Secondly, as you may know, there are global changes that we are experiencing, including the advancement in AI. In the era of artificial intelligence, all industries are being affected and all of these industries need to be connected. At the same time, there is a huge demand for electricity. AI is not only being used in manufacturing, but there is a huge demand for AI data centers. So, on one hand, we are pursuing AI transformation, or AIX. At the same time, we're faced with the need for energy transition. We need a transformation in our electricity grid as well as our power system. For these two reasons, we're now working on changing our economic paradigm. The key is AIX, or AI transformation, on one hand, and energy transformation on the other hand. Our goal on one hand is to become one of the three most powerful AI countries in the world. If we are one of the three, I don't know what the two other countries will be, but our goal is to become one of the top three AI powerhouses in the world. When it comes to physical AI capabilities, we have bold objectives. We want to, if we want to be bold, be number one in terms of physical AI, because we have very strong manufacturing and industrial capabilities. Of all the potential AI capabilities, I believe that we are competitive in terms of physical AI development. Now, when we think about Korea's economic capabilities as they stand right now, I would say that we have been focusing on securing as many GPUs as possible. So far, we have secured more than 260,000 GPUs, which may be more than what we need. At the same time, we are trying to change the way we supply electricity by shifting to renewables. Of course, it will take some time for that transition to happen. But with the war going on in the Middle East, we've realized once again that we need to change our energy paradigm. We do not produce any energy resources; we need to import them, so we are under much pressure. At the same time, we want to turn this crisis into an opportunity. This energy crisis, triggered by the disruptions in the Middle East, can serve as an opportunity for us to accelerate that energy transition. To sum it up, right now the trigger for our innovation-driven economy was changes in our domestic economic system, but we want to be one of the top three AI powerhouses. It sounds like a very clear objective and target that you have set for your country. Now, if you look at this objective of becoming this global AI Hub as a country, what kind of strengths do you see Korea offering to achieve such an objective? 사실 제가 대한민국에 글로벌 AI 허브를 유치하기 위해 정말 열심히 노력했습니다. 유엔 사무총장과 ILO, WHO, IMO 및 기타 유엔 관련 기구들의 수장들을 만나 대한민국에 글로벌 AI 허브를 유치하기 위해 그들을 설득하고 대화했습니다. 하지만 솔직히 말씀드리면 저는 AI 전문가가 아닙니다. 하지만 저는 '글로벌 AI 허브'라는 이름이 아주 멋지다고 생각했습니다. 이름이 참 좋지 않습니까? 그래서 글로벌 AI 허브를 대한민국에 꼭 유치하고 싶었습니다. 하지만 물론 두 가지 근본적인 이유가 있습니다. 첫째, 기술적인 측면에서 대한민국은 크게 기여할 수 있습니다. 둘째, 글로벌 AI 허브가 나아가고자 하는 구체적인 방향과 목표가 있고, 대한민국은 이러한 목표를 실현할 수 있는 공간을 제공할 수 있습니다. 글로벌 AI 허브의 기본 개념은 다음과 같습니다. 세계는 이제 AI 시대로 접어들고 있습니다. 한편으로는 기술적인 변화가 일어나고 있으며, 다른 한편으로는 AI 관련 교육, 규칙, 질서, 윤리, 규제 등 그 뒤를 따르는 다른 모든 측면들을 표준화해야 합니다. 그래서 논의가 필요합니다. 하지만 기술 측면에서 대한민국은 AI와 관련하여 많은 풀스택 역량을 보유하고 있습니다. 그런 점에서 대한민국이 AI에 정말 크게 기여할 수 있다고 생각합니다. 두 번째 이유는 지금의 복잡한 세계 정세를 보면 상대적으로 대한민국은 식민 지배의 경험을 극복하고 선진국으로 성장한 경험이 있습니다. 그리고 AI 생태계를 구축함에 있어 우리는 패권을 추구하거나 그런 태도를 가지지 않을 것입니다. '모두를 위한 AI', 제가 이 슬로건을 직접 제안했습니다. 과거 코로나 시대에 '모두를 위한 백신' 프로그램이 있었던 것처럼, 인류가 나아가야 할 방향이 있다고 생각했습니다. 코로나와 같은 위기가 닥쳤을 때 인류가 백신 개발과 보급을 공유하는 것은 매우 고통스러운 과정이었습니다. 그래서 이 새로운 AI 발전 시대에는 많은 혜택이 있을 것이며, 우리는 이러한 혜택을 공평하게 분배하고 공유할 수 있도록 하고 싶습니다. 대한민국이 이 과정에 기여하고 싶습니다. 그런 관점에서 보면 물론 더 강한 나라들이 있고 대한민국보다 경제 규모가 더 크고 덩치가 큰 나라들도 있습니다. 하지만 다른 참여국들에게 대한민국은 어떤 긴장도 조성하지 않을 것입니다. 우리는 모두가 참여할 수 있는 공간을 제공할 수 있습니다. 그리고 아까 소개해주셨듯이 대한민국의 가장 큰 자부심이 무엇이냐고 묻는다면 여러 가지가 있겠지만, 무엇보다 우리는 원조를 받던 가난한 나라에서 경제 성장을 이룬 것뿐만 아니라, 이른바 'K-민주주의'를 이룩했습니다. 우리 국민 스스로의 힘으로 민주주의를 가능하게 했습니다. 그래서 국민들이 계속해서 민주주의를 성장시키고 있다는 사실, 그 점이 우리가 국제 사회에 기여할 수 있는 부분이며 특히 AI 경제를 성장시키는 데 있어서도 기여할 수 있는 부분입니다. 우리는 이제 막 이 단계를 시작하고 있습니다. 처음에는 5개 국제기구와 논의를 시작했지만, 9개 기구가 서명식에 참석하기 위해 서울에 왔습니다. MDB, 국제기구 및 기타 많은 단체들이 관심을 보였고, 삼성과 같은 한국 기업들도 이 허브에 매우 큰 관심을 가지고 있습니다. 그래서 올해 프로젝트를 시작하고 내년부터 구체적인 내용을 발전시켜 나갈 것입니다. 아시아와 여러 국가의 정치 리더들에게도 계속해서 이 허브에 대해 설명하고 공유하고 있습니다. 우리는 이 허브를 함께 만들어 나갈 것입니다. 아까 말씀드렸듯이 저는 AI 전문가가 아니기에 더 자세한 설명은 드리기 어렵지만, 추가 질문이 있으시면 우리 전문가들을 통해 답변해 드리도록 하겠습니다. 감사합니다. Well, in fact, I really worked hard to attract the Global AI Hub to Korea. I had met with the UN Secretary General and with the ILO, WHO, IMO, and other UN-related agencies. I had met with their heads as well in order to attract the Global AI Hub into Korea. So, I persuaded them and engaged in dialogue with them. But to be honest with you, I'm not an AI expert. But I did believe that, you know, "Global AI Hub"—the name sounds great. It sounds wonderful, right? So, I really wanted to attract the Global AI Hub to Korea. But of course, there are two fundamental reasons. First, in terms of technology, Korea can contribute greatly. Secondly, the Global AI Hub has a specific direction and goal that it hopes to take, and Korea can offer the space to realize these goals. The basic idea behind this hub is the following. The world is now entering the AI era, so technological changes are happening on the one hand. On the other hand, AI-related education, rules, order, ethics, and regulations—we need to standardize all of these other aspects that follow. And so, we need to engage in discussion for that. But in terms of technology, Korea has a lot of full-stack capabilities with regards to AI. In that regard, we feel that Korea can really contribute to AI. The second reason is that looking at the complex global situation right now, relatively speaking, Korea has the experience of overcoming colonial rule and growing to become an advanced country. In building the AI ecosystem, we are not going to pursue hegemony, nor are we going to have any such attitude. "AI for All"—I actually proposed this slogan. I thought of this slogan because during the past COVID era, we had what was called the "Vaccine for All" program. We had that direction for humanity. When there's a crisis such as COVID, for humanity to share in vaccine development and distribution was a very painful process. In this new era of AI development, there will be a lot of benefits, and we want to ensure there will be equitable distribution and sharing of these benefits. Korea hopes to contribute to this process. Seen from that perspective, of course there are stronger countries, countries with a greater economy and a bigger size compared to Korea. However, to the other participating countries, Korea is not going to increase any tension. We can offer the space for everyone to participate. As you introduced earlier, what is the greatest pride of Korea, if you were to ask us this question? There are several, but first of all, we used to be a very poor country but we had great economic growth. Also, the Korean people and Korea, the greatest pride that we have is what is called "K-democracy." We have enabled democracy through the power of the people themselves. The fact that the people are continuing to grow our democracy is an area where we can contribute to the global community, particularly in growing the AI economy. This is where we can contribute, and we are still just beginning this phase. Initially, we had discussions with five international organizations, but nine organizations came to Seoul to participate in the signing ceremony. We had MDBs, international organizations, and many other organizations show their interest. Samsung and other Korean companies are also very much interested in this hub. So, we begin the project this year, and from next year, we will begin to develop the details as well. With the political leaders in Asia and in many other countries as well, I continue to explain to them and share with them, and we will be creating this future, this hub, together. As I mentioned earlier, I'm not an AI expert, so I don't think I can explicate further on that. But if you have additional questions, I will try to address those through our experts. Thank you very much. Thank you. I think what you demonstrate is maybe not strength in AI knowledge, but clearly in leadership to use AI as a force of transformation. Now, while obviously we expect to enjoy the benefits from the development of AI, there have also been concerns about job replacements, job losses, or widening social inequalities. How do you plan to address those and to mitigate those risks? 인류의 역사에서 기술적인 발전이 있을 때마다, 특히 급격한 기술적 돌파구가 마련될 때마다, 한편으로는 인류 전체에 도움이 되었습니다. 하지만 다른 한편으로는 기술 혁신으로 인해 부정적인 영향을 받는 집단이 항상 존재해 왔습니다. 우리가 잘 알다시피 과거에 자동화가 미친 영향도 엄청났습니다. 그래서 대한민국에서도 많은 우려가 있고, 저 또한 개인적으로 AI 발전과 노동 시장에 대해 우려를 가지고 있습니다. AI 발전이 잠재적으로 인간의 일자리를 없앨 수 있다는 우려가 커지고 있습니다. 그래서 최근의 토론은 AI를 긍정적인 기여를 위해 활용하는 방향으로 진행되고 있습니다. 다른 과거의 기술 혁신과 마찬가지로, AI가 사회적 격차와 불평등을 심화시킬 수 있다는 우려가 당연히 있습니다. 그리고 AI가 발전함에 따라 AI 발전에 따른 부와 혜택이 공정하게 분배되지 않을 수도 있습니다. 이것이 우리 고민의 핵심입니다. 물론 우리는 현재 이러한 고민에 대한 명확한 해답을 가지고 있지 않습니다. 우리는 끊임없이 생각하고 고민하고 있습니다. 어떤 면에서 AI 전환의 결과로, 대한민국에는 고성능 반도체 기업들이 있고 그들의 주가가 급격히 상승했습니다. 그래서 주가 상승으로 인해 많은 이익이 발생했습니다. 그리고 이것은 이러한 이익을 사회 전체에 어떻게 분배할 것인가라는 새로운 사회적 문제를 야기했습니다. 이러한 이익이 기업의 주주와 직원들 사이에서만 공유되어야 하는지, 아니면 기업들이 정부의 지원과 납세자들의 돈으로 혜택을 받을 수 있었기 때문에 국민들이나 시민들과도 공유되어야 하는지에 대한 문제입니다. 이것은 한국 사회가 이전에 경험해 보지 못한 새로운 문제이기에 한국 내에서도 상당히 많은 논의가 진행되고 있으며, 아직 이 문제에 대한 해답이나 명확한 답변을 찾지는 못했습니다. 하지만 우리가 지금 집중하고 있는 것은 AI 전환과 관련이 있습니다. 우리는 AI 덕분에 엄청난 혜택과 엄청난 재정적 이익이 발생할 수 있다는 것을 상상할 수 있습니다. 그래서 경제적인 논의들이 있었지만, 이것들은 AI의 혜택을 어떻게 공유할 것인가에 대한 다분히 이론적인 논의들이었습니다. 그리고 우리는 실제로 '기본 소득제'를 적용하는 것을 고려해 볼 수 있을 것입니다. 이재명 정부와 우리 이재명 대통령은 기본 소득제의 잠재적 시행에 관한 제안들을 해왔습니다. 그래서 제가 알기로는 일부 학자나 일부 국가에서 매우 작은 규모로 기본 소득제에 관한 논의와 제안들이 있어 왔습니다. 하지만 지금까지 기본 소득제가 대규모로 시행된 적은 없었습니다. 하지만 우리는 지금 대한민국에서 이 기본 소득 아이디어를 실험하고 있습니다. 예를 들어 농촌 공동체에서 지역 화폐의 형태로 기본 소득을 제공하고 있습니다. 그래서 우리는 기본 소득 개념을 가지고 이러한 실험을 수행하고 있습니다. AI를 통해 창출될 미래의 혜택과 이익도 어떤 형태의 기본 소득제의 형태로 분배될 수 있을 것입니다. 그래서 우리는 우리 사회 내에서 실험을 계속하고 그 결과와 교훈을 전 세계와 공유할 것입니다. 그런 의미에서 우리는 이러한 AI 전환을 겪는 데 있어 선구자가 되고 싶습니다. 왜냐하면 기본 소득, 이 아이디어는 사회 내에서의 경제 성장과 이익의 공정하고 평등한 분배에 관한 것이기 때문입니다. 그래서 우리는 이 문제에 대해 치열하게 고민하고 있으며, 이것은 단지 학술적인 논의가 아니라 정책 차원의 논의이기도 합니다. 그래서 저를 포함한 우리 국무회의에서는 장관들과 저 자신이 이 사회적 실험에 대해 심도 있는 토론을 나누는 단체 채팅방이 있습니다. 그래서 이 우려들에 대한 정답이나 명확한 답변을 가지고 있지는 않지만, 우리는 이러한 많은 아이디어들을 실험하고 있습니다. 감사합니다. Throughout our human history, whenever there's technological advancement, especially when there's dramatic technological breakthroughs, they benefited the entire humanity on one hand. But on the other hand, there had always been some groups within society that were affected negatively by technological innovations. As we may know very well, there was a huge impact from automation in the past as well. Just like any other previous technological innovations, there are of course concerns that AI might worsen the social divide and inequalities. When there is AI development, the wealth and benefits of AI development may not be fairly distributed. That is the core of our concerns. Of course, we don't really have an answer to these concerns at this moment, and we're constantly thinking and pondering upon them. So, a lot of profits were generated from stock price increases. This brought on a new social question of how such profits would be distributed across society. The question is whether these profits should only be shared among the shareholders and the employees of these companies, or whether these profits should also be shared with the people or citizens because these companies were able to benefit from government support and taxpayers' money. This is a new issue that Korean society has never experienced before, so there's quite a lot of debate going on in Korea and we haven't found an answer to this issue yet. But what we're focusing on right now is related to AI transformation. We can imagine that there may be enormous benefits and enormous financial profits to be generated thanks to AI.
